 37: export type BusinessInfoInput = Partial<Omit<InsertBusinessInfo, "id" | "createdAt" | "updatedAt">>;
 38: function normalizeBusinessInfoInput(input: BusinessInfoInput): Omit<InsertBusinessInfo, "createdAt" | "updatedAt"> {
 39:   return {
 40:     id: BUSINESS_INFO_ID,
 41:     ...defaultBusinessInfoValues,
 42:     ...input,
 43:     businessName: input.businessName ?? defaultBusinessInfoValues.businessName,
 44:     legalEntity: input.legalEntity ?? defaultBusinessInfoValues.legalEntity,
 45:     city: input.city ?? defaultBusinessInfoValues.city,
 46:     serviceArea: input.serviceArea ?? defaultBusinessInfoValues.serviceArea,
 47:     primaryPhone: input.primaryPhone ?? defaultBusinessInfoValues.primaryPhone,
 48:     primaryPhoneRaw: input.primaryPhoneRaw ?? defaultBusinessInfoValues.primaryPhoneRaw,
 49:     workingPhone: input.workingPhone ?? defaultBusinessInfoValues.workingPhone,
 50:     workingPhoneRaw: input.workingPhoneRaw ?? defaultBusinessInfoValues.workingPhoneRaw,
 51:     zellePhone: input.zellePhone ?? defaultBusinessInfoValues.zellePhone,
 52:     zellePhoneRaw: input.zellePhoneRaw ?? defaultBusinessInfoValues.zellePhoneRaw,
 53:     primaryEmail: input.primaryEmail ?? defaultBusinessInfoValues.primaryEmail,
 54:     zelleEmail: input.zelleEmail ?? defaultBusinessInfoValues.zelleEmail,
 55:     venmoHandle: input.venmoHandle ?? defaultBusinessInfoValues.venmoHandle,
 56:     stripePaymentLink: input.stripePaymentLink ?? defaultBusinessInfoValues.stripePaymentLink,
 57:     calendarLink: input.calendarLink ?? defaultBusinessInfoValues.calendarLink,
 58:     instagramMain: input.instagramMain ?? defaultBusinessInfoValues.instagramMain,
 59:     instagramCloset: input.instagramCloset ?? defaultBusinessInfoValues.instagramCloset,
 60:     instagramArchive: input.instagramArchive ?? defaultBusinessInfoValues.instagramArchive,
 61:     facebook: input.facebook ?? defaultBusinessInfoValues.facebook,
 62:     poshmarkUrl: input.poshmarkUrl ?? defaultBusinessInfoValues.poshmarkUrl,
 63:     ebayUrl: input.ebayUrl ?? defaultBusinessInfoValues.ebayUrl,
 64:     responseTime: input.responseTime ?? defaultBusinessInfoValues.responseTime,
 65:     hoursNote: input.hoursNote ?? defaultBusinessInfoValues.hoursNote,
 66:     paymentNote: input.paymentNote ?? defaultBusinessInfoValues.paymentNote,
 67:     homeOrganizationSummary: input.homeOrganizationSummary ?? defaultBusinessInfoValues.homeOrganizationSummary,
 68:     legacySummary: input.legacySummary ?? defaultBusinessInfoValues.legacySummary,
 69:     houseCallsSummary: input.houseCallsSummary ?? defaultBusinessInfoValues.houseCallsSummary,
 70:     resaleSummary: input.resaleSummary ?? defaultBusinessInfoValues.resaleSummary,
 71:   };
 72: }
 73: export async function getDb() {
 74:   if (!_db && process.env.DATABASE_URL) {
 75:     try {
 76:       _db = drizzle(process.env.DATABASE_URL);
 77:     } catch (error) {
 78:       console.warn("[Database] Failed to connect:", error);
 79:       _db = null;
 80:     }
 81:   }
 82:   return _db;
 83: }
 84: export async function upsertUser(user: InsertUser): Promise<void> {
 85:   if (!user.openId) {
 86:     throw new Error("User openId is required for upsert");
 87:   }
 88:   const db = await getDb();
 89:   if (!db) {
 90:     console.warn("[Database] Cannot upsert user: database not available");
 91:     return;
 92:   }
 93:   try {
 94:     const values: InsertUser = {
 95:       openId: user.openId,
 96:     };
 97:     const updateSet: Record<string, unknown> = {};
 98:     const textFields = ["name", "email", "loginMethod"] as const;
 99:     type TextField = (typeof textFields)[number];
100:     const assignNullable = (field: TextField) => {
101:       const value = user[field];
102:       if (value === undefined) return;
103:       const normalized = value ?? null;
104:       values[field] = normalized;
105:       updateSet[field] = normalized;
106:     };
107:     textFields.forEach(assignNullable);
108:     if (user.lastSignedIn !== undefined) {
109:       values.lastSignedIn = user.lastSignedIn;
110:       updateSet.lastSignedIn = user.lastSignedIn;
111:     }
112:     if (user.role !== undefined) {
113:       values.role = user.role;
114:       updateSet.role = user.role;
115:     } else if (user.openId === ENV.ownerOpenId) {
116:       values.role = "admin";
117:       updateSet.role = "admin";
118:     }
119:     if (!values.lastSignedIn) {
120:       values.lastSignedIn = new Date();
121:     }
122:     if (Object.keys(updateSet).length === 0) {
123:       updateSet.lastSignedIn = new Date();
124:     }
125:     await db.insert(users).values(values).onDuplicateKeyUpdate({
126:       set: updateSet,
127:     });
128:   } catch (error) {
129:     console.error("[Database] Failed to upsert user:", error);
130:     throw error;
131:   }
132: }
133: export async function getUserByOpenId(openId: string) {
134:   const db = await getDb();
135:   if (!db) {
136:     console.warn("[Database] Cannot get user: database not available");
137:     return undefined;
138:   }
139:   const result = await db.select().from(users).where(eq(users.openId, openId)).limit(1);
140:   return result.length > 0 ? result[0] : undefined;
141: }
142: export async function getBusinessInfo(): Promise<BusinessInfo | undefined> {
143:   const db = await getDb();
144:   if (!db) {
145:     console.warn("[Database] Cannot get business info: database not available");
146:     return undefined;
147:   }
148:   const result = await db.select().from(businessInfo).where(eq(businessInfo.id, BUSINESS_INFO_ID)).limit(1);
149:   return result.length > 0 ? result[0] : undefined;
150: }
151: export async function upsertBusinessInfo(input: BusinessInfoInput): Promise<BusinessInfoInput> {
152:   const db = await getDb();
153:   if (!db) {
154:     console.warn("[Database] Cannot upsert business info: database not available");
155:     return normalizeBusinessInfoInput(input);
156:   }
157:   const values = normalizeBusinessInfoInput(input);
158:   const { id: _id, ...updateSet } = values;
159:   await db.insert(businessInfo).values(values).onDuplicateKeyUpdate({
160:     set: updateSet,
161:   });
162:   return values;
163: }

27: export function patchRecoveredHtml(html: string, filename: string) {
28:   let patched = html
29:     .replaceAll("/assets/logo-black-ihHrkHSC.png", logoStorageUrl)
30:     .replaceAll("logo-black-ihHrkHSC.png", logoStorageUrl)
31:     .replaceAll("/assets/dayna-CD3hSILn.jpg", daynaStorageUrl)
32:     .replaceAll("dayna-CD3hSILn.jpg", daynaStorageUrl)
33:     .replaceAll("https://thewelllivedcitizen.com/services/home-organization", "/services/home-organization")
34:     .replaceAll("https://thewelllivedcitizen.com/services/house-calls", "/services/house-calls")
35:     .replaceAll("https://thewelllivedcitizen.com/services/legacy", "/services/legacy")
36:     .replaceAll("https://thewelllivedcitizen.com/services/resale", "/services/resale")
37:     .replaceAll("https://thewelllivedcitizen.com/services", "/services")
38:     .replaceAll("https://thewelllivedcitizen.com/pricing", "/pricing")
39:     .replaceAll("https://thewelllivedcitizen.com/about", "/about")
40:     .replaceAll("https://thewelllivedcitizen.com/contact", "/contact")
41:     .replaceAll("https://thewelllivedcitizen.com", "/")
42:     .replaceAll("mailto:zelleEmail", "mailto:dayna@thewelllivedcitizen.com");
43:   if (filename === "contact.html") {
44:     patched = patched.replace(
45:       /<script>\s*\(function\(\) \{[\s\S]*?form\.addEventListener\('submit',[\s\S]*?\}\)\(\);\s*<\/script>/,
46:       "",
47:     );
48:   }
49:   return patched;
50: }
51: async function sendRecoveredPage(res: express.Response, filename: string) {
52:   const filePath = path.join(recoveredSiteDir, filename);
53:   const html = await fs.readFile(filePath, "utf8");
54:   res.status(200).type("html").send(patchRecoveredHtml(html, filename));
55: }
56: export function registerRecoveredPublicSite(app: Express) {
57:   app.get("/assets/style-Dbo472dq.css", (_req, res) => {
58:     res.sendFile(path.join(recoveredSiteDir, "style-Dbo472dq.css"));
59:   });
60:   app.get("/info-loader.js", (_req, res) => {
61:     res.type("application/javascript").sendFile(path.join(recoveredSiteDir, "info-loader.js"));
62:   });
63:   app.get("/assets/info-loader.js", (_req, res) => {
64:     res.type("application/javascript").sendFile(path.join(recoveredSiteDir, "info-loader.js"));
65:   });
66:   Array.from(publicPageMap.entries()).forEach(([routePath, filename]) => {
67:     app.get(routePath, async (_req, res, next) => {
68:       try {
69:         await sendRecoveredPage(res, filename);
70:       } catch (error) {
71:         next(error);
72:       }
73:     });
74:   });
75: }

File: well-lived-citizen-site-Claude/server/storage.ts
================
 1: import { ENV } from "./_core/env";
 2: function getForgeConfig() {
 3:   const forgeUrl = ENV.forgeApiUrl;
 4:   const forgeKey = ENV.forgeApiKey;
 5:   if (!forgeUrl || !forgeKey) {
 6:     throw new Error(
 7:       "Storage config missing: set BUILT_IN_FORGE_API_URL and BUILT_IN_FORGE_API_KEY",
 8:     );
 9:   }
10:   return { forgeUrl: forgeUrl.replace(/\/+$/, ""), forgeKey };
11: }
12: function normalizeKey(relKey: string): string {
13:   return relKey.replace(/^\/+/, "");
14: }
15: function appendHashSuffix(relKey: string): string {
16:   const hash = crypto.randomUUID().replace(/-/g, "").slice(0, 8);
17:   const lastDot = relKey.lastIndexOf(".");
18:   if (lastDot === -1) return `${relKey}_${hash}`;
19:   return `${relKey.slice(0, lastDot)}_${hash}${relKey.slice(lastDot)}`;
20: }
21: export async function storagePut(
22:   relKey: string,
23:   data: Buffer | Uint8Array | string,
24:   contentType = "application/octet-stream",
25: ): Promise<{ key: string; url: string }> {
26:   const { forgeUrl, forgeKey } = getForgeConfig();
27:   const key = appendHashSuffix(normalizeKey(relKey));
28:   const presignUrl = new URL("v1/storage/presign/put", forgeUrl + "/");
29:   presignUrl.searchParams.set("path", key);
30:   const presignResp = await fetch(presignUrl, {
31:     headers: { Authorization: `Bearer ${forgeKey}` },
32:   });
33:   if (!presignResp.ok) {
34:     const msg = await presignResp.text().catch(() => presignResp.statusText);
35:     throw new Error(`Storage presign failed (${presignResp.status}): ${msg}`);
36:   }
37:   const { url: s3Url } = (await presignResp.json()) as { url: string };
38:   if (!s3Url) throw new Error("Forge returned empty presign URL");
39:   const blob =
40:     typeof data === "string"
41:       ? new Blob([data], { type: contentType })
42:       : new Blob([data as any], { type: contentType });
43:   const uploadResp = await fetch(s3Url, {
44:     method: "PUT",
45:     headers: { "Content-Type": contentType },
46:     body: blob,
47:   });
48:   if (!uploadResp.ok) {
49:     throw new Error(`Storage upload to S3 failed (${uploadResp.status})`);
50:   }
51:   return { key, url: `/manus-storage/${key}` };
52: }
53: export async function storageGet(relKey: string): Promise<{ key: string; url: string }> {
54:   const key = normalizeKey(relKey);
55:   return { key, url: `/manus-storage/${key}` };
56: }
57: export async function storageGetSignedUrl(relKey: string): Promise<string> {
58:   const { forgeUrl, forgeKey } = getForgeConfig();
59:   const key = normalizeKey(relKey);
60:   const getUrl = new URL("v1/storage/presign/get", forgeUrl + "/");
61:   getUrl.searchParams.set("path", key);
62:   const resp = await fetch(getUrl, {
63:     headers: { Authorization: `Bearer ${forgeKey}` },
64:   });
65:   if (!resp.ok) {
66:     const msg = await resp.text().catch(() => resp.statusText);
67:     throw new Error(`Storage signed URL failed (${resp.status}): ${msg}`);
68:   }
69:   const { url } = (await resp.json()) as { url: string };
70:   return url;
71: }

 4: 
 5: | Field | Current Working Value | Status | Notes |
 6: |---|---|---|---|
 7: | Business name | The Well Lived Citizen | Working | Directly supplied in Dayna’s latest review block. |
 8: | Legal entity | Well Dressed Citizen LLC | Working | Directly supplied in Dayna’s latest review block. |
 9: | Primary domain | thewelllivedcitizen.com | Working | Treated as active domain. |
10: | Alias domain | welllivedcitizen.com | Working | Marked as also owned and mirroring the primary site. |

15: | Closet Instagram | @thewelllivedcloset | Working | Directly supplied in Dayna’s latest review block. |

21:

That should be carried forward as a working operational fact, while the older number remains in the system as a separate issue to resolve rather than as the default published number.

File: well-lived-citizen-site-Claude/dashboard-build-order.md
================
 1: # Internal Dashboard Build Order
 2: 
 3: ## Build Principle
 4: 
 5: The first live version should reduce Dayna’s cognitive load immediately. That means the earliest release should prioritize capture, visibility, and continuity before automation flourishes.
 6: 
 7: ## Phase 1 MVP
 8: 
 9: | Module | Why It Comes First | Required Capability |
10: |---|---|---|
11: | Today | Gives Dayna a clean landing surface with open asks, recent updates, and what is waiting on her | Read aggregated dashboard state |
12: | Business Facts | Establishes the single source of truth for contact, services, socials, payments, and core business identity | Create and edit structured fields |
13: | Requests and Needs | Makes visible what the system still needs from Dayna and what has already been resolved | Checklist tracking |
14: | Intake | Lets Dayna drop raw updates into the system so they can be structured quickly | Fast note capture with interpretation fields |
15: 
16: ## Phase 2 Operational Continuity
17: 
18: | Module | Why It Comes Second | Required Capability |
19: |---|---|---|
20: | Voice and Brand | Preserves wording, tone, and positioning consistency across sessions and agents | Editable brand rules |
21: | Handoffs | Packages approved facts and next actions for other agents or future sessions | Generate exportable handoff packet |
22: | Activity History | Creates auditability across changes and interpretations | Timestamped update log |
23: 
24: ## Phase 3 Enhancements
25: 
26: | Module | Why It Comes Later | Required Capability |
27: |---|---|---|
28: | Prompt Builder | Useful once the source of truth is stable | Convert approved data into agent-ready prompts |
29: | Smart intake suggestions | Helpful, but only after enough examples exist | Pattern-based suggestions from prior structured entries |
30: | Cross-surface publishing | Useful after the internal model is stable | Controlled export into other tools or systems |
31: 
32: ## Non-Negotiable UX Rule
33: 
34: The dashboard must always feel simpler than the underlying data model. If a feature helps developers but makes Dayna think harder, it belongs behind the scenes rather than in the primary interface.

File: well-lived-citizen-site-Claude/dashboard-model-notes.md
================
1: # Dashboard Model Notes
2: 
3: The internal dashboard should now treat three distinct objects as separate concerns rather than one blended form. First, it needs a **facts layer** for stable business values such as business name, legal entity, main email, social handles, and the currently preferred phone number. Second, it needs a **decision layer** for unresolved routing and operational questions such as redirect behavior or what to do with a failing legacy number. Third, it needs a **review layer** that presents those facts and decisions in mobile-friendly tap controls rather than requiring repeated voice correction.
4: 
5: At the current stage, the working facts set supports beginning the dashboard build with a clean intake surface and a review queue. The most important near-term modeling decision is that **310-993-0204** should be treated as the current working contact number, while **323-433-1350** should remain visible only as an operational issue to resolve. That distinction prevents the interface from publishing a failing number while still preserving the context Dayna supplied.

File: well-lived-citizen-site-Claude/fact-check-narrative-template.md
================
 1: # Fact-Check Narrative Template
 2: 
 3: ## Purpose
 4: 
 5: This format turns a build-agent audit into a fast mobile review flow for Dayna. It is designed for voice reply, not long typing. Each item should present the current believed fact, why it matters, and the fastest response path: **yes**, **no**, or **corrected value**.
 6: 
 7: ## Review Rules
 8: 
 9: | Rule | Application |
10: |---|---|
11: | One fact per item | Avoid stacked questions that force repeated clarification. |
12: | Plain language first | Use business language, not technical labels, on the visible layer. |
13: | Correction-friendly | Every item must be answerable with a short spoken correction. |
14: | Confidence visible behind the scenes | The system should preserve whether the fact came from Dayna, the build agent, or a noisy file. |
15: | Only ask what is needed | Do not make Dayna reapprove facts already confirmed directly. |
16: 
17: ## Item Structure
18: 
19: | Field | Meaning |
20: |---|---|
21: | Category | Contact, social, payments, service, domain, brand, or workflow |
22: | Proposed fact | What the system currently believes is true |
23: | Source | Where the fact came from |
24: | Confidence | High, medium, or low |
25: | Voice review prompt | Short sentence Dayna can answer by voice |
26: | Accepted responses | Yes, no, or corrected value |
27: | Update behavior | What the dashboard should do after Dayna replies |
28: 
29: ## Example Review Items
30: 
31: | Category | Proposed Fact | Source | Confidence | Voice Review Prompt | Accepted Responses | Update Behavior |
32: |---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
33: | Contact | The main phone number is 3234331350. | Repeated in prior instruction and JSON reference | High | Is 3234331350 still the main phone number? | Yes / No / New phone number | If yes, mark confirmed. If corrected, replace and timestamp. |
34: | Contact | The main email is dayna@thewelllivedcitizen.com. | JSON reference | Medium | Is dayna@thewelllivedcitizen.com still the right main email? | Yes / No / New email | If corrected, replace and mark prior value superseded. |
35: | Social | The main Instagram is @thewelllivedcitizen. | JSON reference and prior instruction | High | Is @thewelllivedcitizen still the main Instagram? | Yes / No / New handle | Update active social record. |
36: | Workflow | The old-domain redirect should still be set up. | Prior task brief only | Low | Do we still care about redirecting the old co domain, or is that dead? | Yes / No / Clarifying note | If no, retire the item from active asks. |
37: 
38: ## Mobile Review Pattern
39: 
40: The ideal mobile screen should show a short stack of review cards. Each card should present a single statement and three clear actions: confirm, correct, or defer. The interface should minimize typing and let Dayna move quickly through a queue of facts from the builder or from noisy sources.
41: 
42: ## Output After Review
43: 
44: After Dayna responds, the system should produce three outputs at once: an updated source-of-truth record, a resolved-or-pending checklist update, and a clean handoff note for the build agent.

File: well-lived-citizen-site-Claude/internal-dashboard-spec.md
================
 1: # The Well Lived Citizen — Internal Living Dashboard Spec
 2: 
 3: ## Product Intent
 4: 
 5: The internal dashboard is a private operating layer for Dayna. It is not a developer console and not a public website. Its job is to capture authoritative business facts, translate Dayna’s voice-text and brain dumps into clean structured records, maintain a current brand and business source of truth, and prepare reliable handoffs for separate execution agents.
 6: 
 7: ## Trust Boundary
 8: 
 9: | Rule | Implementation Consequence |
10: |---|---|
11: | Clean-start reset is active. | No legacy company files, historical repositories, old dashboards, or prior agent assumptions are valid unless Dayna explicitly reintroduces them. |
12: | Dayna is the authority. | Direct user messages and explicitly approved uploads become the source of truth. |
13: | Voice-to-text errors are normal. | The system should favor contextual interpretation and only surface clarification requests when ambiguity would materially change meaning. |
14: | Dashboard serves humans and builders. | The interface must feel simple to Dayna while the underlying data stays structured enough for downstream development use. |
15: 
16: ## Core Screens
17: 
18: | Screen | Purpose | Primary User Value |
19: |---|---|---|
20: | Today | Show open asks, pending inputs, active decisions, and recent updates. | Immediate calm and visibility. |
21: | Business Facts | Store current business name, contact data, domain, hours, services, social links, and payment links. | Single source of truth. |
22: | Voice and Brand | Capture tone rules, phrasing preferences, banned language, and approved positioning. | Consistency across sessions and agents. |
23: | Intake | Convert Dayna’s raw updates into structured entries with source attribution and timestamps. | Fast capture from voice-text and brain dumps. |
24: | Handoffs | Generate clean transfer packets for implementation agents or future sessions. | Continuity without drift. |
25: | Requests and Needs | Track what the system is waiting on from Dayna and what has already been resolved. | Clear checklist and reduced mental load. |
26: 
27: ## Data Domains
28: 
29: | Domain | Required Fields | Notes |
30: |---|---|---|
31: | Business identity | businessName, ownerName, legalEntity, description, domain | Treat each field as independently editable and timestamped. |
32: | Contact | primaryPhone, primaryEmail, contactPreference, responseTime, bookingLink | Direct-use values should support downstream website wiring. |
33: | Social | instagramMain, instagramSecondary, facebook, otherActiveChannels | Keep inactive or retired channels separately marked, not mixed into active ones. |
34: | Payments | zelle, venmo, stripe, invoiceInstructions, paymentNotes | Values should distinguish handle, link, and usage notes. |
35: | Services | serviceName, serviceSummary, status, pricingMode, notes | Structured enough to inform both content and operations. |
36: | Brand voice | toneRules, approvedPhrases, bannedPhrases, audienceNotes, formattingRules | Must preserve Dayna’s working language. |
37: | Session inputs | rawInput, interpretedMeaning, confidence, sourceType, timestamp | Maintains traceability from brain dump to structured record. |
38: | Handoff packets | objective, approvedFacts, openQuestions, blockedItems, nextPrompt | Enables cross-agent continuity. |
39: 
40: ## Input-to-Structure Workflow
41: 
42: | Step | System Behavior |
43: |---|---|
44: | Capture | Dayna provides a brain dump, correction, or new business fact. |
45: | Interpret | The system normalizes obvious transcription issues and extracts operational meaning. |
46: | Structure | The update is written into the correct domain with timestamp and source note. |
47: | Confirm by behavior | If ambiguity is low, the dashboard updates directly. If ambiguity is material, the system asks a focused follow-up question. |
48: | Publish internally | Updated facts become available to downstream prompts, handoffs, and implementation work. |
49: 
50: ## Checklist Logic
51: 
52: The dashboard should maintain a visible checklist of open asks and dependencies. That list should separate what the system needs from Dayna, what is blocked by another agent or system, and what has already been translated into structured truth. The point is not project management theater. The point is reducing cognitive load and preventing repeated asks.
53: 
54: | Checklist Section | Meaning |
55: |---|---|
56: | Waiting on Dayna | Facts or decisions only Dayna can supply |
57: | In progress | Information currently being structured or implemented |
58: | Ready for handoff | Clean outputs available for another agent to use |
59: | Resolved | Items already incorporated into the dashboard |
60: 
61: ## UX Direction
62: 
63: The interface should feel closer to an iOS operating companion than a back-office admin panel. It should read clearly, minimize clutter, and let Dayna move quickly between capture, review, and handoff. It should use plain language labels rather than technical system terms. The visible structure should help her think, not force her to think like a developer.
64: 
65: ## Developer Layer
66: 
67: Under the surface, the dashboard should preserve stable schemas, timestamps, and attribution fields so implementation agents can consume the information safely. The interface may feel soft and human, but the data underneath should be rigid enough to support APIs, prompts, content generation, and execution workflows without ambiguity.
68: 
69: ## Immediate Open Questions
70: 
71: | Question | Why It Matters |
72: |---|---|
73: | What are the current authoritative business facts for contact, domain, services, socials, and payments? | These populate the initial source of truth. |
74: | What should the first live version prioritize: intake, facts, handoffs, or all four major screens? | This determines the minimum viable dashboard. |
75: | Should the dashboard support direct prompt generation for other agents from day one? | This affects the handoff workflow design. |
76: | Does Dayna want the dashboard optimized first for desktop, mobile, or both equally? | This sets layout priorities. |

File: well-lived-citizen-site-Claude/mobile-review-packet.md
================
 1: # Mobile Review Packet
 2: 
 3: This packet translates Dayna’s latest working fact set into a faster mobile review model. The goal is to replace long voice correction loops with tap-friendly confirmation patterns. Each row is written so it can become a checkbox, segmented control, or short correction field inside the internal dashboard.
 4: 
 5: ## Working Fact Set
 6: 
 7: | # | Category | Working Fact | Confidence | Recommended Mobile Control | Options or Expected Input |
 8: |---|---|---|---|---|---|
 9: | 1 | Business identity | The business name is **The Well Lived Citizen**. | High | Checkbox | Keep as-is / Edit text |
10: | 2 | Legal entity | The legal entity is **Well Dressed Citizen LLC**. | High | Checkbox | Keep as-is / Edit text |
11: | 3 | Primary domain | The active domain is **thewelllivedcitizen.com**. | High | Checkbox | Keep as-is / Edit text |
12: | 4 | Domain alias | **welllivedcitizen.com** is also owned and mirrors the primary site. | High | Multiple choice | Keep mirror / Change routing / Remove |
13: | 5 | Primary contact number | Use **310-993-0204** as the personal mobile contact. | High | Multiple choice | Keep personal mobile / Replace with new number / Mark as unresolved |
14: | 6 | Main email | The main email is **dayna@thewelllivedcitizen.com**. | Medium | Checkbox | Keep as-is / Edit text |
15: | 7 | Main Instagram | The main Instagram is **@thewelllivedcitizen**. | High | Checkbox | Keep as-is / Edit handle |
16: | 8 | Closet Instagram | The closet Instagram is **@thewelllivedcloset**. | High | Checkbox | Keep as-is / Edit handle |
17: | 9 | Facebook | The Facebook handle is **/thewelllivedcitizen**. | High | Checkbox | Keep as-is / Edit handle |
18: | 10 | Zelle destination | Zelle points to **dayna@thewelllivedcitizen.com**. | High | Multiple choice | Keep current email / Change to another email / Change to another tag |
19: | 11 | Redirect behavior | A redirect decision is still needed for the legacy domain or legacy destination behavior. | Medium | Multiple choice | Redirect to primary domain / Redirect to Resell & Consignment page / Remove redirect item |
20: 
21: ## UI Translation
22: 
23: The fastest mobile interaction model is not one giant form. It should be a review queue with a short statement, one primary confirmation action, and one alternate correction path. Straight facts such as the business name, legal entity, and social handles should use a simple **keep or edit** pattern. Routing, phone, and payment items should use **multiple-choice controls** because they imply a decision rather than a pure text correction.
24: 
25: ## Normalization Notes
26: 
27: | Item | Normalization Decision |
28: |---|---|
29: | 5 | The phone decision has been rewritten as a routing choice rather than preserving the longer note about Google Voice and AT&T plan changes inside the visible fact field. That note should live in internal metadata, not in the user-facing fact card. |
30: | 8 | The phrase about using “gorgeous” styling assets appears unrelated to the social handle itself, so it should be treated as a separate design/archive note rather than a correction to the closet Instagram field. |
31: | 10 | The note about Zelle tags has been preserved as an alternate-path decision and should be stored as payment metadata if needed. |
32: | 11 | The original line appears malformed and mixes redirect intent with a search URL. It has been normalized into a cleaner redirect decision that can still be resolved later without carrying forward broken wording. |
33: 
34: ## Implementation Direction
35: 
36: Inside the living dashboard, this packet should become a **Review** surface with three behaviors. Confirmed items should immediately move into the current source of truth. Edited items should store both the new value and the superseded value with a timestamp. Unresolved items should move to the requests or blockers queue instead of staying mixed into confirmed facts.

File: well-lived-citizen-site-Claude/vite.config.ts

  1: import { jsxLocPlugin } from "@builder.io/vite-plugin-jsx-loc";
  2: import tailwindcss from "@tailwindcss/vite";
  3: import react from "@vitejs/plugin-react";
  4: import fs from "node:fs";
  5: import path from "node:path";
  6: import { defineConfig, type Plugin, type ViteDevServer } from "vite";
  7: import { vitePluginManusRuntime } from "vite-plugin-manus-runtime";
  8: const PROJECT_ROOT = import.meta.dirname;
  9: const LOG_DIR = path.join(PROJECT_ROOT, ".manus-logs");
 10: const MAX_LOG_SIZE_BYTES = 1 * 1024 * 1024;
 11: const TRIM_TARGET_BYTES = Math.floor(MAX_LOG_SIZE_BYTES * 0.6);
 12: type LogSource = "browserConsole" | "networkRequests" | "sessionReplay";
 13: function ensureLogDir() {
 14:   if (!fs.existsSync(LOG_DIR)) {
 15:     fs.mkdirSync(LOG_DIR, { recursive: true });
 16:   }
 17: }
 18: function trimLogFile(logPath: string, maxSize: number) {
 19:   try {
 20:     if (!fs.existsSync(logPath) || fs.statSync(logPath).size <= maxSize) {
 21:       return;
 22:     }
 23:     const lines = fs.readFileSync(logPath, "utf-8").split("\n");
 24:     const keptLines: string[] = [];
 25:     let keptBytes = 0;
 26:     const targetSize = TRIM_TARGET_BYTES;
 27:     for (let i = lines.length - 1; i >= 0; i--) {
 28:       const lineBytes = Buffer.byteLength(`${lines[i]}\n`, "utf-8");
 29:       if (keptBytes + lineBytes > targetSize) break;
 30:       keptLines.unshift(lines[i]);
 31:       keptBytes += lineBytes;
 32:     }
 33:     fs.writeFileSync(logPath, keptLines.join("\n"), "utf-8");
 34:   } catch {
 35:   }
 36: }
 37: function writeToLogFile(source: LogSource, entries: unknown[]) {
 38:   if (entries.length === 0) return;
 39:   ensureLogDir();
 40:   const logPath = path.join(LOG_DIR, `${source}.log`);
 41:   const lines = entries.map((entry) => {
 42:     const ts = new Date().toISOString();
 43:     return `[${ts}] ${JSON.stringify(entry)}`;
 44:   });
 45:   fs.appendFileSync(logPath, `${lines.join("\n")}\n`, "utf-8");
 46:   trimLogFile(logPath, MAX_LOG_SIZE_BYTES);
 47: }
 48: function vitePluginManusDebugCollector(): Plugin {
 49:   return {
 50:     name: "manus-debug-collector",
 51:     transformIndexHtml(html) {
 52:       if (process.env.NODE_ENV === "production") {
 53:         return html;
 54:       }
 55:       return {
 56:         html,
 57:         tags: [
 58:           {
 59:             tag: "script",
 60:             attrs: {
 61:               src: "/__manus__/debug-collector.js",
 62:               defer: true,
 63:             },
 64:             injectTo: "head",
 65:           },
 66:         ],
 67:       };
 68:     },
 69:     configureServer(server: ViteDevServer) {
 70:       server.middlewares.use("/__manus__/logs", (req, res, next) => {
 71:         if (req.method !== "POST") {
 72:           return next();
 73:         }
 74:         const handlePayload = (payload: any) => {
 75:           if (payload.consoleLogs?.length > 0) {
 76:             writeToLogFile("browserConsole", payload.consoleLogs);
 77:           }
 78:           if (payload.networkRequests?.length > 0) {
 79:             writeToLogFile("networkRequests", payload.networkRequests);
 80:           }
 81:           if (payload.sessionEvents?.length > 0) {
 82:             writeToLogFile("sessionReplay", payload.sessionEvents);
 83:           }
 84:           res.writeHead(200, { "Content-Type": "application/json" });
 85:           res.end(JSON.stringify({ success: true }));
 86:         };
 87:         const reqBody = (req as { body?: unknown }).body;
 88:         if (reqBody && typeof reqBody === "object") {
 89:           try {
 90:             handlePayload(reqBody);
 91:           } catch (e) {
 92:             res.writeHead(400, { "Content-Type": "application/json" });
 93:             res.end(JSON.stringify({ success: false, error: String(e) }));
 94:           }
 95:           return;
 96:         }
 97:         let body = "";
 98:         req.on("data", (chunk) => {
 99:           body += chunk.toString();
100:         });
101:         req.on("end", () => {
102:           try {
103:             const payload = JSON.parse(body);
104:             handlePayload(payload);
105:           } catch (e) {
106:             res.writeHead(400, { "Content-Type": "application/json" });
107:             res.end(JSON.stringify({ success: false, error: String(e) }));
108:           }
109:         });
110:       });
111:     },
112:   };
113: }
114: const plugins = [react(), tailwindcss(), jsxLocPlugin(), vitePluginManusRuntime(), vitePluginManusDebugCollector()];
115: export default defineConfig({
116:   plugins,
117:   resolve: {
118:     alias: {
119:       "@": path.resolve(import.meta.dirname, "client", "src"),
120:       "@shared": path.resolve(import.meta.dirname, "shared"),
121:       "@assets": path.resolve(import.meta.dirname, "attached_assets"),
122:     },
123:   },
124:   envDir: path.resolve(import.meta.dirname),
125:   root: path.resolve(import.meta.dirname, "client"),
126:   publicDir: path.resolve(import.meta.dirname, "client", "public"),
127:   build: {
128:     outDir: path.resolve(import.meta.dirname, "dist/public"),
129:     emptyOutDir: true,
130:   },
131:   server: {
132:     host: true,
133:     allowedHosts: [
134:       ".manuspre.computer",
135:       ".manus.computer",
136:       ".manus-asia.computer",
137:       ".manuscomputer.ai",
138:       ".manusvm.computer",
139:       "localhost",
140:       "127.0.0.1",
141:     ],
142:     fs: {
143:       strict: true,
144:       deny: ["**/.*"],
145:     },
146:   },

 1: # ZIP Triage Summary
 2: 
 3: ## What the ZIP Actually Contains
 4: 
 5: The uploaded archive does not contain a clean site build, page assets, or deployable source code. It contains five reference files only: a task brief, a task-branch note, a skill file, a business-info JSON reference, and a site-audit note.
 6: 
 7: ## What Is Usable
 8: 
 9: | Item | Status | Reason |
10: |---|---|---|
11: | Business name: The Well Lived Citizen | Salvageable | Repeated consistently across the brief, branch note, and JSON reference. |
12: | Legal entity: Well Dressed Citizen LLC | Salvageable | Repeated consistently across the brief, branch note, and JSON reference. |
13: | Domain: thewelllivedcitizen.com | Salvageable but still user-confirmed preferred | Repeated consistently in the brief and branch note. |
14: | Primary phone: 3234331350 | Salvageable | Present in the JSON reference and aligned with prior direct instruction. |
15: | Primary email: dayna@thewelllivedcitizen.com | Salvageable pending Dayna override | Present in the JSON reference. |
16: | Instagram main: @thewelllivedcitizen | Salvageable | Present in the JSON reference and prior task statements. |
17: | Instagram closet: @thewelllivedcloset | Salvageable | Present in the JSON reference and prior task statements. |
18: | Facebook: /thewelllivedcitizen | Salvageable | Present in the JSON reference and prior task statements. |
19: | Response note: Within 24 hours. Text for urgent requests. | Tentatively salvageable | Present in the JSON reference, but should remain editable. |
20: 
21: ## What Is Not Safe to Treat as Truth
22: 
23: | Item | Status | Reason |
24: |---|---|---|
25: | Any extracted or live-site-derived file state | Not trusted | The brief and audit both warn that Replit-era files may be questionable after April 17. |
26: | Requirement to use the live site or extracted files as the build source | Rejected | The brief explicitly says Dayna must identify what is clean rather than the system assuming it. |
27: | Old-domain redirect requirement | Needs confirmation | It appears in the brief and branch note, but the audit says no old-domain references were found in the extracted site. |
28: | Claims about current page correctness from curl extraction | Informational only | Those findings came from a workflow already marked as questionable. |
29: | Any implication that this ZIP is a clean rebuild source | Rejected | The archive contains references, not actual deployable files. |
30: 
31: ## Operational Conclusion
32: 
33: This ZIP is useful as a **reference bundle**, not as a build bundle. It helps recover candidate business facts and prior warnings, but it should not be treated as authoritative implementation source code. The clean workflow remains: salvage repeated facts, route anything uncertain into a fact-check narrative, and let Dayna confirm or correct by voice once rather than repeating the whole project history.
